href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="infobox vevent" season</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" class="hlist noprint nowrap" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane seasons</a><br />\n<a href="/wiki/2015_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2015 Atlantic hurricane season">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2016 Atlantic hurricane season">2016</a>, <b>2017</b>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">2018</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">2019</a></i></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>2017 Atlantic hurricane season</b> is an ongoing event in the annual formation of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic basin">Atlantic basin</a>. The season has been hyperactive,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> featuring both the highest total <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">accumulated cyclone energy</a> (ACE) and the highest number of major hurricanes since <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>. It has the greatest number of consecutive hurricanes in the satellite era, with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin_(2017)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Franklin (2017)">Franklin</a> through <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">Ophelia</a> all reaching winds of at least 75&#160;mph (120&#160;km/h). In addition, it has thus far been a very destructive season and likely the costliest on record, with a preliminary total of over $188 billion (<a href="/wiki/United_states_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="United states dollar">USD</a>) in damages, nearly all of which was due to three of the major hurricanes of the season \xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Harvey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Maria</a>. This season is also <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes#Systems" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">one of only six years</a> on record to feature multiple Category&#160;5 hurricanes. Irma\'s landfall on <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> and Maria\'s landfall on <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> make 2017 the second season on record (after <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007</a>) to feature two hurricanes making landfall at Category&#160;5 intensity. In addition, Irma was the strongest hurricane ever recorded to form in the Atlantic Ocean outside of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This season is the only season on record in which three hurricanes each had an <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">ACE</a> of over 40: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Jose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Maria</a>. The season also featured <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">Ophelia</a>, the easternmost major hurricane in the basin on record, the strongest storm to make landfall in Ireland in modern times, and the most damaging storm to impact <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> since <a href="/wiki/Great_Storm_of_1987" title="Great Storm of 1987">1987</a>.</p>\n<p>The season officially began on June&#160;1 and will end on November&#160;30. These dates historically describe the period of year when most tropical cyclones form in the Atlantic basin and are adopted by convention. However, as shown by <a href="#Tropical_Storm_Arlene">Tropical Storm Arlene</a> in April, the formation of tropical cyclones is possible at other times of the year. Arlene also marked 2017 the third consecutive year to feature a pre-season storm. In mid-June, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">Tropical Storm Bret</a> struck the island of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, which is only rarely struck by tropical cyclones due to its low latitude. A few days later, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">Tropical Storm Cindy</a> struck the state of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>. In late August, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a> became the first major hurricane to make landfall in the United States since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, while also setting the record for most rainfall dropped by a tropical cyclone in the US. In early September, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_hurricane" title="Cape Verde hurricane">Cape Verde-type hurricane</a>, became the first <a href="/wiki/Category_5_hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Category 5 hurricane">Category 5&#160;hurricane</a> to impact the northern <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> on record, as well as equaling the strongest hurricane ever to make landfall in the Atlantic basin\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">1935 Labor Day hurricane</a>. With <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> striking <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> as a top-end Category&#160;4, the season was the first on record to feature three Atlantic hurricanes making landfall anywhere in the United States or one of its territories at Category&#160;4 intensity or stronger. The season also featured the fastest tropical cyclone ever recorded in the Gulf of Mexico (<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nate_(2017)" title="Hurricane Nate (2017)">Nate</a>). This was the first season to have three hurricanes make landfall in the mainland United States (Harvey, Irma, and Nate) since <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008</a>, and the first season to feature four hurricanes making landfall in the overall United States (Harvey, Irma, Maria, and Nate) since <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>.</p>\n<p>Beginning in 2017, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) has the option to issue advisories, and thus allow watches and warnings to be issued, on disturbances that are not yet tropical cyclones but have a high chance to become one, and are expected to bring tropical storm or hurricane conditions to landmasses within 48&#160;hours. Such systems are termed "potential tropical cyclones". Advisories on these storms contain the same content, including track forecasts and cyclone watches and warnings, as advisories on active tropical cyclones.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The first storm to receive this designation was Potential Tropical Cyclone Two, which later developed into <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">Tropical Storm Bret</a>, east-southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> on June&#160;18.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> In addition, the numbering that a potential tropical cyclone receives would be retained for the rest of the hurricane season, meaning that the next tropical system would be designated with the following number, even though potential tropical cyclones do not qualify as tropical cyclones. This was first demonstrated with <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Other_systems" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">Potential Tropical Cyclone Ten</a>, which failed to develop into a tropical cyclone.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Seasonal_forecasts"><span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Other_systems"><span class="tocnumber">3.17</span> <span class="toctext">Other systems</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a <span class="toctext">Season effects</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_forecasts">Seasonal forecasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Seasonal forecasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toccolours" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="3" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; text-align:right; clear: />\nhurricanes</span></b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;" colspan="2"><i>Average <span style="font-size: 80%;">(1981\xe2\x80\x932010<sup id="cite_ref-Background_5-0" id="cite_ref-Aug17TSR_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aug17TSR-19">[19]</a></sup></td>\n<td align="left">August 4, 2017</td>\n<td>17</td>\n<td>7</td>\n<td>3</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/NOAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NOAA">NOAA</a><sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_midOutlook_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_midOutlook-20">[20]</a></sup></td>\n<td align="left">August 9, 2017</td>\n<td>14\xe2\x80\x9319</td>\n<td>5\xe2\x80\x939</td>\n<td>2\xe2\x80\x935</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="6" style="text-align:center;">\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"></td>\n<td align="left"><b>Actual activity</b><br /></td>\n<td>15</td>\n<td>10</td>\n<td>6</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;" colspan="5">* June\xe2\x80\x93November only.<br />\n\xe2\x80\xa0 Most recent of several such occurrences. (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_records#Seasonal_activity" title="List of Atlantic hurricane records">See all</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Ahead of and during the season, several national meteorological services and scientific agencies forecast how many named storms, hurricanes and major (Category&#160;3 or higher on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a>) hurricanes will form during a season and/or how many tropical cyclones will affect a particular country. These agencies include the Tropical Storm Risk (TSR) Consortium of the University College London, the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA) and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a> (CSU). The forecasts include weekly and monthly changes in significant factors that help determine the number of tropical storms, hurricanes, and major hurricanes within a particular year.<sup id="cite_ref-Dec17TSR_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dec17TSR-6">[6]</a></sup> Some of these forecasts also take into consideration what happened in previous seasons and the dissipation of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9316_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event</a>. On average, an Atlantic hurricane season between 1981 and 2010 contained twelve tropical storms, six hurricanes, and two major hurricanes, with an <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) index of between 66 and 103&#160;units.<sup id="cite_ref-Background_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Background-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-season_outlooks">Pre-season outlooks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-season outlooks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first forecast for the year was issued by TSR on December 13, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Dec17TSR_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dec17TSR-6">[6]</a></sup> They anticipated that the 2017 season would be a near-average season, with a prediction of 14 named storms, 6 hurricanes, and 3 major hurricanes. They also predicted an ACE index of around 101&#160;units.<sup id="cite_ref-Dec17TSR_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dec17TSR-6">[6]</a></sup> On December 14, CSU released a qualitative discussion detailing five possible scenarios for the 2017 season, taking into account the state of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Multidecadal_Oscillation" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Multidecadal Oscillation">Atlantic Multidecadal Oscillation</a> and the possibility of <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o">El Ni\xc3\xb1o</a> developing during the season.<sup id="cite_ref-Dec17CSU_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dec17CSU-21">[21]</a></sup> TSR lowered their forecast numbers on April 5, 2017 to 11 named storms, 4 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes, based on recent trends favoring the development of El Ni\xc3\xb1o.<sup id="cite_ref-Apr17TSR_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apr17TSR-7">[7]</a></sup> The next day, CSU released their prediction, also predicting a total of 11 named storms, 4 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes.<sup id="cite_ref-Apr17CSU_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apr17CSU-8">[8]</a></sup> On April 17, <a href="/wiki/The_Weather_Company" title="The Weather Company">The Weather Company</a> released their forecasts, calling for 2017 to be a near-average season, with a total of 12 named storms, 6 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes.<sup id="cite_ref-Apr17TWC_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apr17TWC-9">[9]</a></sup> The next day, on April 18, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">North Carolina State University</a> released their prediction, also predicting a near-average season, with a total of 11\xe2\x80\x9315 named storms, 4\xe2\x80\x936 hurricanes, and 1\xe2\x80\x933 major hurricanes.<sup id="cite_ref-Apr17NCSU_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apr17NCSU-10">[10]</a></sup> On May 20, The Weather Company issued an updated forecast, raising their numbers to 14 named storms, 7 hurricanes, and 3 major hurricanes to account for Tropical Storm Arlene as well as the decreasing chance of El Ni\xc3\xb1o forming during the season.<sup id="cite_ref-May17TWC_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-May17TWC-11">[11]</a></sup> On May 25, NOAA released their prediction, citing a 70% chance of an above average season due to "a weak or nonexistent El Ni\xc3\xb1o", calling for 11\xe2\x80\x9317 named storms, 5\xe2\x80\x939 hurricanes, and 2\xe2\x80\x934 major hurricanes.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-12">[12]</a></sup> On May 26, TSR updated its prediction to around the same numbers as its December 2016 prediction, with only a minor change in the expected ACE index amount to 98&#160;units.<sup id="cite_ref-May17TSR_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-May17TSR-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-season_outlooks">Mid-season outlooks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mid-season outlooks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>CSU updated their forecast on June 1 to include 14 named storms, 6 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes, to include Tropical Storm Arlene.<sup id="cite_ref-June17CSU_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-June17CSU-14">[14]</a></sup> It was based on the current status of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Oscillation" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Oscillation">North Atlantic Oscillation</a>, which was showing signs of leaning towards a negative phase, favoring a warmer tropical Atlantic; and the chances of El Ni\xc3\xb1o forming were significantly lower. However, they stressed on the uncertainty that the <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o%E2%80%93Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x93Southern Oscillation">El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x93Southern Oscillation</a> could be in a warm-neutral phase or weak El Ni\xc3\xb1o conditions by the peak of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-June17CSU_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-June17CSU-14">[14]</a></sup> On the same day, the United Kingdom <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a> (UKMO) released its forecast of a very slightly above-average season. It predicted 13 named storms, with a 70% chance that the number would be in the range between 10 and 16, and 8 hurricanes, with a 70% chance that the number would be in the range between 6 and 10. It also predicted an ACE index of 145, with a 70% chance that the index would be between 92 and 198.<sup id="cite_ref-June17UKMO_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-June17UKMO-15">[15]</a></sup> On July 4, TSR released their fourth forecast for the season, increasing their predicted numbers to 17 named storms, 7 hurricanes, and 3 major hurricanes, due to the fact that El Ni\xc3\xb1o conditions would no longer develop by the peak of the season and the warming of sea-surface temperatures across the basin. Additionally, they predicted a revised ACE index of 116&#160;units.<sup id="cite_ref-Jul17TSR_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jul17TSR-16">[16]</a></sup> During August 9, NOAA released their final outlook for the season, raising their predictions to 14\xe2\x80\x9319 named storms, though retaining 5\xe2\x80\x939 hurricanes and 2\xe2\x80\x935 major hurricanes. They also stated that the season had the potential to be extremely active, possibly the most active since <a href="/wiki/2010_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2010 Atlantic hurricane season">2010</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_midOutlook_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_midOutlook-20">[20]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season">Timeline of the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season</a></div>\n<center>\n<div tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Katia,_Irma,_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg/330px-Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg" width="330" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg/495px-Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg/660px-Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9200" data-file-height="5175" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Katia,_Irma,_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThree simultaneous hurricanes active on September 8, with <a href="#Hurricane_Katia">Katia</a> <i>(left)</i>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a> <i>(center)</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Jose</a> <i>(right)</i>. All three were threatening land at the time.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Atlantic hurricane season officially began on June 1, 2017, although activity began earlier for the third consecutive year since <a href="/wiki/2015_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2015 Atlantic hurricane season">2015</a>. Roughly a month before the official start, the first storm, <a href="#TS_Arlene">Arlene</a>, developed on April 19 in the northern Atlantic Ocean. It was the first named storm to develop in the month of April since <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Ana in 2003</a>. In June, two more tropical storms developed: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">Bret</a>, which affected areas in the southeastern Caribbean Sea, including <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">Cindy</a>, which formed in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> less than a day after Bret had developed. In July, a tropical depression developed in the Main Development Region (MDR), the second tropical cyclone to develop in the MDR before the month of August, after Bret, and was followed by Tropical Storm Don. At the end of that month, a cold front stalled over the Gulf of Mexico and portions of the southeastern United States, spawning Tropical Depression Six, which quickly developed into Tropical Storm Emily.<sup id="cite_ref-nhc_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhc-22">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<p>August featured the season\'s first hurricane, Franklin, which formed in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Campeche" title="Bay of Campeche">Bay of Campeche</a>. A few days after Franklin dissipated, Tropical Storm Gert formed northeast of the Bahamas, eventually becoming a hurricane at a high latitude over the western Atlantic. On August 17, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Tropical Storm Harvey</a> formed east of the Windward Islands, before opening up into a wave over the central Caribbean three days later. Harvey then regenerated into a tropical depression over the southwestern Gulf of Mexico on August 23, and rapidly strengthened into a Category&#160;4 hurricane before making landfall near <a href="/wiki/Rockport,_Texas" title="Rockport, Texas">Rockport, Texas</a>, late on August 25. Harvey became the first major hurricane to make landfall in the United States since Wilma in 2005, the first Category&#160;4 hurricane to make landfall in Texas since Carla in 1961, and the first Category&#160;4 hurricane landfall in the contiguous United States since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">Charley</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-nhc_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhc-22">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; clear: right;">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="3"><b>Most intense Atlantic<br />\nhurricane seasons</b><br />\n<small>(since 1850)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[nb 1]</a></sup></small></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Rank</th>\n<th><a season">2005</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">250</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>3</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">1893</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">231</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>4</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/1926_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1926 Atlantic hurricane season">1926</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">230</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>5</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/1995_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1995 Atlantic hurricane season">1995</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">228</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>6</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">227</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>7</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">2017</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">221</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>8</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/1950_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1950 Atlantic hurricane season">1950</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">211</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>9</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/1961_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1961 Atlantic hurricane season">1961</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">205</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>10</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">1998</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">182</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n<div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Hurricane_Tracks_from_2017_with_Precipitation_and_Cloud_Data.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Tracks_from_2017_with_Precipitation_and_Cloud_Data.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n2017 Atlantic Hurricane storm tracks with IMERG precipitation and GOES clouds (from August&#160;10 to September&#160;23).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>September featured copious activity. Irma formed in the Eastern Atlantic and rapidly intensified into a Category&#160;5 hurricane east of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>. Irma is the strongest hurricane in terms of sustained winds since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a> in 2005, and the strongest hurricane outside of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and Gulf of Mexico on record. While Irma impacted the northern Leeward Islands, Hurricane Jose formed on September 5, peaking as a high-end Category&#160;4 hurricane before weakening and making an anti-cyclonic loop in the northern Atlantic Ocean. When Katia formed, 2017 became the first year since <a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">1998</a> in which six hurricanes have formed in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> On September 17, Maria became a Category&#160;5 hurricane, threatening the same areas devastated by Hurricane Irma. When Lee intensified into a major hurricane on September 27, it became the first time in seven years that five major hurricanes formed. Activity briefly paused as September came to a close.</p>\n<p>Activity resumed on October 4, when Tropical Depression Sixteen formed in the Southwestern Caribbean Sea, which strengthened into Tropical Storm Nate on the next day as it neared the coast of Nicaragua. Nate strengthened to a hurricane on October 7, and made two landfalls in the United States as a Category 1 hurricane - the first near the mouth of the Mississippi River in southeastern Louisiana late on October 7 and the second near Biloxi, Mississippi early October 8. As Nate became a post-tropical cyclone on October 9, Tropical Depression Seventeen formed in the eastern subtropical Atlantic, strengthening into Tropical Storm Ophelia that same day. Ophelia became a hurricane two days later, marking the first time since <a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">1893</a> that 10 consecutive named storms strengthened into hurricanes. On October 14, Ophelia unexpectedly strengthened into a major hurricane, becoming the sixth major hurricane of the season and the easternmost major hurricane in the Atlantic basin on record.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">accumulated cyclone energy</a> (ACE) index for the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season, as of 21:00&#160;UTC on October&#160;15, is 220.718&#160;units,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[nb 2]</a></sup> which is one of the highest values on record for an Atlantic hurricane season as well as the most since 2005, and more than double the 1981\xe2\x80\x932010 full-season median of 92 units. With an ACE value under 4&#160;units following the dissipation of Emily, 2017 set the record for lowest ACE produced by a season\'s first five named storms.<sup id="cite_ref-FirstFive_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirstFive-28">[26]</a></sup> Despite that, the 2017 season hosted the storm with the third-highest ACE value (Hurricane Irma, at 66.6 units) and is one of only four seasons (including <a href="/wiki/1966_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1966 Atlantic hurricane season">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2003 Atlantic hurricane season">2003</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a>) to have at least two hurricanes with an ACE value over 40 and the only season to have had three.<sup id="cite_ref-ACE40three_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACE40three-29">[27]</a></sup> 2017 also hosted the day with the most ACE produced (September 8) and currently has the <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy#Atlantic_basin_ACE" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">fourth highest ACE value of any Atlantic season since 1950</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nhc_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhc-22">[22]</a></sup> September also generated the highest ACE value for any month in the Atlantic, surpassing September&#160;2004.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> ACE is, broadly speaking, a measure of the power of the hurricane multiplied by the length of time it existed, so storms that last a long time, as well as particularly strong hurricanes, have high ACEs. It is only calculated for full advisories on tropical systems at or exceeding 39&#160;mph (63&#160;km/h), which is tropical storm strength.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Arlene">Tropical Storm Arlene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Arlene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Arlene 2017-04-20 1512Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg/150px-Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg/225px-Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg/300px-Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="3600" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Arlene_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Arlene 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Arlene_2017_track.png/150px-Arlene_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Arlene_2017_track.png/225px-Arlene_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Arlene_2017_track.png/300px-Arlene_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>April 19&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 April 21</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>50&#160;mph (85&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 990&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes">List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes</a></div>\n<p>A potent <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> formed well east of Bermuda on April&#160;16. The cyclone moved southeast, becoming disconnected from the surrounding environment and gradually losing its frontal characteristics. Deep <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">convection</a> formed in <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">bands</a> north and east of the center by 00:00&#160;UTC on April&#160;19, leading to the formation of a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical depression</a>. Despite an unfavorable environment, with ocean temperatures near 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and moderate <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, convection coalesced near the center and allowed the subtropical depression to become fully tropical by 00:00&#160;UTC on April&#160;20. It intensified into Tropical Storm Arlene six hours later. After attaining peak winds of 50&#160;mph (85&#160;km/h), the storm began to rotate around a larger extratropical low. The storm tracked into the cold sector of the cyclone, causing Arlene to lose tropical characteristics around 12:00&#160;UTC on April&#160;21. The post-tropical cyclone moved south and east, before dissipating well west-southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> on April&#160;22.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Upon its formation as a subtropical depression on April&#160;19, Arlene was the sixth known subtropical or tropical cyclone to form in the month of <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes">April</a> in the Atlantic basin; the other instances were Ana in 2003, a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_Storm_One_(1992)" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical Storm One (1992)">subtropical storm in April 1992</a>, and three tropical depressions in 1912, 1915, and 1973, respectively. When Arlene became a tropical storm on April&#160;20, this marked only the second such occurrence on record, after Ana in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-TWC_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWC-32">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[nb 3]</a></sup> Furthermore, it had the lowest central pressure of any Atlantic storm recorded in the month of April, with a central pressure of 990&#160;mbar (hPa; 29.23&#160;inHg), again surpassing Ana.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> Additionally, unrelated to Arlene, <a href="/wiki/2017_PHS#Tropical_Storm_Adrian" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 PHS">Tropical Storm Adrian</a> in the Eastern Pacific basin also formed before the corresponding hurricane season was set to officially begin, being the earliest named storm in the Eastern Pacific proper. The last time where the first storms in both basins were pre-season storms was in <a href="/wiki/2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2016 Atlantic hurricane season">2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Bret">Tropical Storm Bret</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Bret">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Bret 2017-06-19 Suomi NPP.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg" width="150" height="210" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2265" data-file-height="3175" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Bret_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Bret 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bret_2017_track.png/150px-Bret_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bret_2017_track.png/225px-Bret_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bret_2017_track.png/300px-Bret_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 19&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 June 20</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1007&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">Tropical Storm Bret (2017)</a></div>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> on June 13 and was first monitored by the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> shortly afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> Development, however, was expected to be slow due to its low latitude and relatively fast motion. As it moved swiftly across the Main Development Region of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, the disturbance began to gradually organize, and the NHC raised development chances slightly on June 16.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> Little change in organization occurred until June 18, at which point a burst of <a href="/wiki/Convection" title="Convection">convection</a> near the center of the disturbance prompted the NHC to designate the system as Potential Tropical Cyclone Two at 21:00&#160;UTC. This was the agency\'s first designation of a disturbance that had not yet developed into a tropical cyclone.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> The storm continued to organize as it accelerated towards <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and Trinidad and Tobago throughout the night, with banding features becoming evident. Later on June 19, the system developed a closed low-level circulation and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Bret at 21:00&#160;UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup> One day later, at 21:00&#160;UTC on June 20, the last advisory on Bret was issued following its degeneration into a tropical wave.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to Phil Klotzbach of Colorado State University, Bret was the earliest storm to form in the Main Development Region on record, surpassing a record set by <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(1979)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Ana (1979)">Tropical Storm Ana</a> in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> Bret was also the lowest latitude named storm in the month of June since <a href="/wiki/1933_Trinidad_hurricane" title="1933 Trinidad hurricane">1933</a> at 9.4\xc2\xb0N.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, one person died after he slipped and fell while running across a makeshift bridge; the fatality is considered indirectly related to Bret.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> Another fatality occurred in Tobago after a man\'s house collapsed on him; he eventually succumbed to his injuries a week later.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Cindy">Tropical Storm Cindy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Cindy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Cindy 2017-06-21 1645Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg/150px-Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg" width="150" height="192" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg/225px-Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg/300px-Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="6400" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Cindy_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Cindy 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cindy_2017_track.png/150px-Cindy_2017_track.png" width="150" height="95" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cindy_2017_track.png/225px-Cindy_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cindy_2017_track.png/300px-Cindy_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1900" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 20&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 June 23</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>60&#160;mph (95&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 992&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)</a></div>\n<p>The NHC first began monitoring the potential for tropical cyclone formation over the northwestern Caribbean Sea on June&#160;13.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> A large area of disturbed weather developed within the region three days later,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> and it slowly organized while entering the central Gulf of Mexico, prompting the NHC to begin advisories on a potential tropical cyclone on June&#160;19. The structure of the system was initially sprawling, with tropical storm-force winds well displaced from a broad area of low pressure with embedded swirls.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> A reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system around 18:00&#160;UTC the following day was able to pinpoint a well-defined center, indicating the formation of Tropical Storm Cindy.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup> Despite the presence of dry air and strong wind shear, the cyclone still managed to attain peak winds of 60&#160;mph (95&#160;km/h) before weakening on approach to the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> It made landfall between <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Texas" title="Port Arthur, Texas">Port Arthur, Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cameron,_Louisiana" title="Cameron, Louisiana">Cameron, Louisiana</a> early on June&#160;22 and weakened while progressing inland.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A state of emergency was declared for <a href="/wiki/Biloxi,_Mississippi" title="Biloxi, Mississippi">Biloxi, Mississippi</a> in anticipation of flooding. A ten-year-old boy died from injuries sustained during the storm in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Morgan,_Alabama" title="Fort Morgan, Alabama">Fort Morgan, Alabama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> A second fatality later occurred in <a href="/wiki/Bolivar_Peninsula,_Texas" title="Bolivar Peninsula, Texas">Bolivar Peninsula, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Four">Tropical Depression Four</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Four">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="04L 2017-07-06 1605Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg/150px-04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg" width="150" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg/225px-04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg/300px-04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6488" data-file-height="8601" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:04L_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="04L 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/04L_2017_track.png/150px-04L_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/04L_2017_track.png/225px-04L_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/04L_2017_track.png/300px-04L_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 6&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 7</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>30&#160;mph (45&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1008&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Early on June&#160;29, the NHC began tracking a tropical wave embedded within a large envelope of deep moisture across the coastline of western Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> The disturbance was introduced as a potential contender for tropical cyclone formation two days later, as environmental conditions were expected to favor slow organization.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> It began to show signs of organization over the central Atlantic early on July&#160;3,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> but the chances for development began to decrease two days later as the system moved toward a more stable environment.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> Having already acquired a well-defined circulation, the development of a persistent mass of deep convection around 03:00&#160;UTC the following day prompted the NHC to upgrade the wave to Tropical Depression Four, located about 1,545&#160;miles (2,485&#160;km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> Despite wind shear being low, the nascent depression struggled to intensify due to a dry environment caused by a <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Air_Layer" title="Saharan Air Layer">Saharan Air Layer</a> to its east, causing the low-level circulation to weaken, and resulting in the tropical depression degenerating into an open tropical wave late on the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Don">Tropical Storm Don</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Don">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Don 2017-07-18 1718Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg/150px-Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg" width="150" height="195" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg/225px-Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg/300px-Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2672" data-file-height="3472" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Don_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Don 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Don_2017_track.png/150px-Don_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Don_2017_track.png/225px-Don_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Don_2017_track.png/300px-Don_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 17&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 19</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>50&#160;mph (85&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1007&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Late on July&#160;15, the NHC highlighted a low-pressure trough over the central Atlantic as having the potential to develop into a tropical cyclone in the coming days.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> The disturbance began to show signs of organization early on July&#160;17,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> and data from a reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system confirmed the development of Tropical Storm Don around 21:00&#160;UTC that day.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> The storm\'s overall appearance improved over subsequent hours up until around 09:00 UTC, as a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a>, accompanied by significant clusters of lightning, became pronounced.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[61]</a></sup> Don attained its peak intensity at this time, characterised by winds of approximately 50&#160;mph (85&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[61]</a></sup> The next plane to investigate the cyclone a few hours later, however, found that the system\'s center had become less defined, and that sustained wind speeds had decreased to about 40&#160;mph (65&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> A combination of reconnaissance data and surface observations from the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> indicated that Don opened up into a tropical wave around 03:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;19, as it entered the eastern Caribbean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Emily">Tropical Storm Emily</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Emily">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Emily 2017-07-31 1555Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/150px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/225px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/300px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Emily_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Emily 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/150px-Emily_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/225px-Emily_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/300px-Emily_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 31&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1005&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In late July, a dissipating <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">cold front</a> extended into the northeastern Gulf of Mexico, where the NHC began forecasting the development of an area of low pressure over the next day on July&#160;30. Any development was expected to be slow due to land proximity and marginal upper-level winds.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> Contrary to predictions, a rapid period of organization occurred over the next 24 hours and the system was deemed as Tropical Depression Six at 09:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;31,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> strengthening into Tropical Storm Emily just two hours later. After attaining its peak intensity with winds of 45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) and a minimum pressure of 1,005&#160;<a href="/wiki/Millibar" class="mw-redirect" title="Millibar">mbar</a> (29.7&#160;<a href="/wiki/Inches_of_mercury" class="mw-redirect" title="Inches of mercury">inHg</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> Emily made landfall on <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Island" title="Anna Maria Island">Anna Maria Island</a> around 14:45&#160;UTC. Weakening quickly ensued, and later that day the circulation of Emily became elongated as it was downgraded to a tropical depression.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> The increasingly disrupted system later moved off the <a href="/wiki/First_Coast" title="First Coast">First Coast</a> of Florida into the western Atlantic early the next day, accelerating northeastwards before becoming embedded within a frontal zone early on August&#160;2.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Following the classification of Tropical Storm Emily, Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> for 31&#160;counties to ensure residents were provided with the necessary resources.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> The storm spawned an EF0 tornado near Bradenton. The tornado was on the ground for about 1.3&#160;mi (2.1&#160;km) and destroyed two barns and a few greenhouses, while an engineered wall collapsed, leaving about $96,000 in damage.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> On August&#160;1, torrential rains related to Emily impacted parts of <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami Beach">Miami Beach</a>, with accumulations reaching 6.97&#160;in (177&#160;mm) in 3.5&#160;hours, of which 2.17&#160;in (55&#160;mm) fell in just 30&#160;minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> Coinciding with high tide the deluge overwhelmed flood pumps, with three of them shutting down due to lightning-induced power outages, and resulted in significant flash floods. Multiple buildings suffered water damage, with some having 2.5&#160;ft (0.76&#160;m) of standing water. One person was hospitalized after becoming stuck in flood waters.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> Portions of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Downtown_Miami" title="Greater Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Brickell" title="Brickell">Brickell</a>, were also heavily affected; numerous vehicles became stranded in flooded roadways.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Franklin">Hurricane Franklin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Franklin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Franklin 2017-08-09 1854Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/150px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg" width="150" height="209" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/225px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/300px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2501" data-file-height="3480" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Franklin 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Franklin_2017_track.png/150px-Franklin_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Franklin_2017_track.png/225px-Franklin_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Franklin_2017_track.png/300px-Franklin_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 7&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>85&#160;mph (140&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 981&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin" title="Hurricane Franklin">Hurricane Franklin</a></div>\n<p>The NHC began tracking a tropical wave in the southeastern Caribbean Sea for possible <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">development</a> on August 3.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> After organizing for a few days, advisories were initiated on Potential Tropical Cyclone Seven at 21:00&#160;UTC on August 6.<sup id="cite_ref-d1_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-d1-79">[76]</a></sup> The disturbance became Tropical Storm Franklin at 03:00&#160;UTC on August 7.<sup id="cite_ref-d2_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-d2-80">[77]</a></sup> After strengthening into a moderate tropical storm, Franklin made its first landfall near Pulticub, Mexico at 03:00&#160;UTC on August 8.<sup id="cite_ref-1stlandfallfranklin_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1stlandfallfranklin-81">[78]</a></sup> The cyclone weakened considerably while over the peninsula, however its satellite presentation remained well-defined, with the inner core tightening up considerably.<sup id="cite_ref-d7_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-d7-82">[79]</a></sup> Later that day, Franklin emerged into the Bay of Campeche, and immediately began strengthening again, becoming a hurricane late on August&#160;9.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup> Five hours after peaking in intensity with winds of 85&#160;mph (140&#160;km/h) and a pressure of 981&#160;mbar (28.97&#160;inHg),<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup> Franklin made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Vega_de_Alatorre" title="Vega de Alatorre">Lechuguillas, Mexico</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> and thereafter began to rapidly weaken. By 15:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;10, Franklin had dissipated as a tropical cyclone.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> However, its mid-level circulation remained intact and later contributed to the formation of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Jova_(2017)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Jova (2017)">Tropical Storm Jova</a> in the Eastern Pacific early on August&#160;12.<sup id="cite_ref-Jova_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jova-87">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Immediately upon classification of Franklin as a potential tropical cyclone, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm_warning" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm warning">tropical storm warnings</a> were issued for much of the eastern side of the Yucat\xc3\xa1n Peninsula on August 6;<sup id="cite_ref-d1_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-d1-79">[76]</a></sup> a small portion of the coastline was upgraded to a hurricane watch with the possibility of Franklin nearing hurricane intensity as it approached the coastline the next night. Approximately 330 people were reported as going into storm shelters, and around 2,200 relocated from the islands near the coastline to farther inland in advance of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-impacts1_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impacts1-88">[85]</a></sup> In the Mexican part of the peninsula, damage was reported as having being minimal, mainly in Belize as the storm tracked slightly more northwards then expected, lessening impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-impacts1_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impacts1-88">[85]</a></sup> Nonetheless, some areas received up to a foot of rain.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Gert">Hurricane Gert</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Gert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Gert 2017-08-16 Suomi NPP.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg" width="150" height="218" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2270" data-file-height="3300" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Gert_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Gert 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gert_2017_track.png/150px-Gert_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gert_2017_track.png/225px-Gert_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gert_2017_track.png/300px-Gert_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1669" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 13&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 17</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>105&#160;mph (165&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 967&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On August&#160;2, the NHC began monitoring a tropical wave and its associated convection over the western coast of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> As the disturbance tracked west-northwest, its structure changed little in organization, but environmental conditions were expected to support the formation of a tropical cyclone.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup> Instead, the system remained poorly defined and entered a less conducive environment east of the Leeward Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> After progressing into the southwestern Atlantic several days later, the wave encountered more favorable upper-level winds and began to show signs of organization.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> Following the formation of a well-defined circulation, the disturbance was upgraded to a tropical depression at 03:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;13;<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> by 21:00&#160;UTC that afternoon, it intensified into Tropical Storm Gert.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup> At 03:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;15, Gert intensified to a Category&#160;1 hurricane with maximum sustained winds of 75&#160;mph (120&#160;km/h), making it the second hurricane of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> Accelerating east-northeastwards, Gert peaked as a Category&#160;2 system early on August&#160;17 at an unusually high latitude of 40\xc2\xb0N.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> Thereafter, Gert began to rapidly weaken as it shifted from the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> over cooler waters.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> Just 12&#160;hours after achieving peak intensity, Gert weakened below hurricane status and evolved to an extratropical cyclone well east of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Two people drowned due to strong rip currents produced by the hurricane: one in the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a> of North Carolina, and the other in <a href="/wiki/Nantucket,_Massachusetts" title="Nantucket, Massachusetts">Nantucket, Massachusetts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hurricane Harvey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png" class="image"><img alt="Harvey 2017-08-25 2231Z.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png/150px-Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png/225px-Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png/300px-Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="2400" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Harvey_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Harvey 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Harvey_2017_track.png/150px-Harvey_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Harvey_2017_track.png/225px-Harvey_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Harvey_2017_track.png/300px-Harvey_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 17&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>130&#160;mph (215&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 938&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a></div>\n<p>The NHC began monitoring an area of low pressure southwest of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> on August 13, which was expected to merge with a tropical wave that just emerged off the coast of Africa, within a few days.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> Instead the two systems remained separate,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> with the first low pressure area coalescing into a potential tropical cyclone by 15:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;17.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup> A reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system was able to locate a well-defined circulation, and the disturbance was upgraded to Tropical Storm Harvey accordingly six hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup> On a westward course into the Caribbean Sea, the storm was plagued by relentless wind shear, and it degenerated to an open tropical wave south of Hispaniola, by 03:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;20.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup> Harvey\'s remnants continued into the Bay of Campeche, where more conducive environmental conditions led to the re-designation of a tropical depression, around 15:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;23, and subsequent intensification into a tropical storm by 04:00&#160;UTC on the next morning.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup> The tropical cyclone began a period of rapid intensification shortly thereafter, attaining hurricane intensity by 17:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;24,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-109">[106]</a></sup> Category&#160;3 strength around 19:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;25,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> and Category&#160;4 intensity by 23:00&#160;UTC on that day.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-109">[106]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Harvey crossed the shore between <a href="/wiki/Port_Aransas,_Texas" title="Port Aransas, Texas">Port Aransas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_O%27Connor,_Texas" title="Port O\'Connor, Texas">Port O\'Connor, Texas</a> around 03:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;26, possessing maximum winds of 130&#160;mph (215&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup> The storm gradually spun down, becoming a tropical storm around 18:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;26, as it meandered across southeastern Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup> A light steering pattern caused the storm to emerge into the Gulf of Mexico on August&#160;28,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup> but a turn toward the north-northeast brought it ashore west of Cameron, Louisiana, as a weak tropical storm around 09:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;30.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup> The system weakened to a tropical depression over central Louisiana late that day before losing tropical characteristics over central Tennessee early on September&#160;1.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[113]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rockport, <a href="/wiki/Fulton,_Texas" title="Fulton, Texas">Fulton</a>, and the surrounding cities bore the brunt of Harvey\'s eyewall as it moved ashore in Texas. Numerous structures were heavily damaged or destroyed, boats were tossed or capsized, power poles were leant or snapped, and trees were downed. As debris covered roadways and cellphone service was compromised, communication to the hardest-hit locales was severed. One person was killed in Rockport after a fire began in his home, and approximately a dozen people were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-twc_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twc-117">[114]</a></sup> Farther northeast, dire predictions of potentially catastrophic flooding came to fruition in <a href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston, Texas">Houston</a> and nearby locales, where floodwaters submerged interstates, forced residents to their attics and roofs, and overwhelmed emergency lines. The National Weather Service <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a>, "This event is unprecedented &amp; all impacts are unknown &amp; beyond anything experienced..." At least 30 people were killed in the Houston area due to flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-TNYT_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-118">[115]</a></sup> In addition to the flooding, Harvey spawned several tornadoes around Houston.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[116]</a></sup> Preliminary estimates place the damage caused by Harvey between $65<sup
