id="cite_ref-AIR_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIR-120">[117]</a></sup> and $200 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-200billion_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200billion-121">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Quealy_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quealy-122">[119]</a></sup> Harvey killed 90 people, including 1 in <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a><sup id="cite_ref-cdema_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdema-123">[120]</a></sup> and 89 in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WashPost_death_toll_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashPost_death_toll-125">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[124]</a></sup> The storm produced 64.58 in (1,640&#160;mm) of rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, the highest-ever rainfall total for any tropical cyclone in the United States and the third-highest rainfall total for a tropical cyclone in the Atlantic basin.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[nb 4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Harvey was the first major hurricane to strike the United States since Hurricane Wilma in 2005, ending the record-length 4,323-day span in which no tropical cyclones made landfall as major hurricanes.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[126]</a></sup> It is the most intense tropical cyclone to move ashore the US mainland since Hurricane Charley in 2004, and the first Category&#160;4 hurricane to make landfall in Texas since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carla" title="Hurricane Carla">Hurricane Carla</a> in <a href="/wiki/1961_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1961 Atlantic hurricane season">1961</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[127]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Irma">Hurricane Irma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hurricane Irma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Irma 2017-09-06 1745Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg/150px-Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg/225px-Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg/300px-Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="9600" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Irma 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/150px-Irma_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/225px-Irma_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/300px-Irma_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1669" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 30&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 12</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>185&#160;mph (295&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 914&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a></div>\n<p>A westward-moving tropical wave, first monitored over western Africa on August&#160;26,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[128]</a></sup> organized into Tropical Storm Irma around 15:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;30.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[129]</a></sup> Amid an environment of low wind shear and warm ocean temperatures, the newly formed cyclone moved generally westward while intensifying. A reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system east of the Caribbean on September&#160;5 found the cyclone at Category&#160;5 intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[130]</a></sup> With a clear eye surrounded by a ring of extremely deep convection, Irma attained its peak intensity with winds of 185&#160;mph (295&#160;km/h) later that day,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[131]</a></sup> and maintained this intensity as it moved through the northern Leeward Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[132]</a></sup> Some weakening occurred south of the Bahamas,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup> but the cyclone regained Category&#160;5 intensity before making landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Sabana-Camag%C3%BCey_Archipelago" title="Sabana-Camag\xc3\xbcey Archipelago">Sabana-Camag\xc3\xbcey Archipelago</a> of Cuba around 03:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;9.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[134]</a></sup> Land interaction disrupted the storm temporarily,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup> but once again it strengthened to acquire winds of 130&#160;mph (215&#160;km/h), before making landfall in <a href="/wiki/Cudjoe_Key,_Florida" title="Cudjoe Key, Florida">Cudjoe Key</a> of the Florida Keys early on September&#160;10.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup> A few hours later, it struck <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">Marco Island, Florida</a>, with winds of 115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[137]</a></sup> Irma continued north and west, steadily weakening over the Southeastern United States before losing tropical characteristics in Georgia, early on September&#160;12.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup></p>\n<p>With peak winds of 185&#160;mph (295&#160;km/h), Irma is the strongest Atlantic storm outside of the Gulf of Mexico or Caribbean Sea on record, and is the 11th most intense hurricane on record in the Atlantic basin. Maintaining peak intensity for 37 consecutive hours, Irma is the only tropical cyclone on record worldwide to have had winds that intense for so long. As the storm moved through the northern Leeward Islands, it became the only Category&#160;5 to make a direct impact there; its landfall intensity ties it with the 1935 Labor Day hurricane as the strongest landfalling cyclone on record in the Atlantic. Two Category&#160;4 hurricanes, Harvey and Irma, struck the continental United States in the span of two weeks; this marks the first time the country has suffered two landfalls of such intensity during the same hurricane season, in recorded history. Lastly, Irma accrued the third-highest Accumulated Cyclone Energy index on record.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the aftermath of Irma, development on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> was described as being "95% destroyed" by respective political leaders, with 1,400 people feared homeless in Barbuda.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup> So far, Irma has resulted in at least 134 deaths, including 44 across the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, and 90 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_death_toll_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_death_toll-145">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nuclear_landscape_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuclear_landscape-146">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-World_AFP_death_toll_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_AFP_death_toll-147">[143]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Jose">Hurricane Jose</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hurricane Jose">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Jose 2017-09-08 1425Z (cropped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="150" height="213" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="454" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Jose_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Jose 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jose_2017_track.png/150px-Jose_2017_track.png" width="150" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jose_2017_track.png/225px-Jose_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jose_2017_track.png/300px-Jose_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2513" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 5&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 22</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>155&#160;mph (250&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 938&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose (2017)</a></div>\n<p>A westward-moving tropical wave exited the west coast of Africa on August&#160;31,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> organizing into Tropical Storm Jose over the open eastern Atlantic by 15:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;5.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup> The quickly-strengthening cyclone attained hurricane intensity late on September&#160;6,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[146]</a></sup> reached major hurricane strength late on September&#160;7,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[147]</a></sup> and ultimately peaked as a Category&#160;4 with winds of 155&#160;mph (250&#160;km/h) early on September&#160;9.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[148]</a></sup> Moderate wind shear weakened the cyclone as it conducted a slow clockwise loop between Bermuda and the Caribbean Sea and eventually moved north ahead of an approaching trough.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[149]</a></sup> Steering currents collapsed by early on September&#160;21, causing the system to stall offshore the Northeastern United States as a weakening tropical storm.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[150]</a></sup> With a rain shield in the northern and northwestern semicircles accompanied by a lack of deep convection over the center, the NHC declared Jose a post-tropical cyclone around 03:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;22, ending advisories once the storm\'s tropical storm-force winds moved off the New England coast at 21:00 UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The government of <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a> began efforts on September 8 to evacuate the entire island of Barbuda prior to Jose\'s anticipated arrival, as most structures on the island had been heavily damaged or destroyed by Hurricane Irma.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[153]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Katia">Hurricane Katia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hurricane Katia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Katia 2017-09-08 1930Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg/150px-Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg" width="150" height="194" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg/225px-Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg/300px-Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4536" data-file-height="5872" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Katia_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Katia 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Katia_2017_track.png/150px-Katia_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Katia_2017_track.png/225px-Katia_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Katia_2017_track.png/300px-Katia_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 5&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 9</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>105&#160;mph (165&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 972&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A trough was present over the southwestern Gulf of Mexico on September&#160;3, producing a widespread area of thunderstorms.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[154]</a></sup> Two days later, a distinct low pressure area formed about 50&#160;mi (80&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Tampico" title="Tampico">Tampico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[155]</a></sup> At 21:00&#160;UTC that day, the NHC designated the system as Tropical Depression Thirteen after an organized area of convection formed over the center. Located in an area of weak steering currents, the depression drifted slowly eastward. With gradually decreasing wind shear and warm water temperatures, the system intensified into Tropical Storm Katia on September&#160;6, as the convection became better organized.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[157]</a></sup> Later that day, an aircraft reconnaissance flight into the storm found a partial <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye wall</a> and surface winds of 76&#160;mph (122&#160;km/h); on that basis, the NHC upgraded Katia to hurricane status.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[158]</a></sup> The convection organized into a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> as the system stalled.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[159]</a></sup> Late in the evening of September 8, Katia made landfall north of <a href="/wiki/Tecolutla" title="Tecolutla">Tecolutla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> as a weak Category&#160;1 storm.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[160]</a></sup> The system rapidly dissipated over land on September 9. Katia\'s remnants traveled across Central America and later emerged over the Pacific Ocean, where redevelopment ensued. Tropical Depression Fifteen-E formed, which later strengthened into <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Otis_(2017)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Otis (2017)">Hurricane Otis</a> about a week later.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[161]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In preparation for Katia, over 4,000 residents were evacuated from the states of <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[162]</a></sup> Tourists left coastal towns, emergency shelters were opened, and storm drains were cleared before the onset of heavy rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[163]</a></sup> Two fatalities were reported in <a href="/wiki/Xalapa" title="Xalapa">Xalapa</a> from mudslides, while a third man was swept away by floodwaters in <a href="/wiki/Jalcomulco" title="Jalcomulco">Jalcomulco</a>. States of emergency were declared for 40 out of a total 53 municipalities that reported minor damage from mudslides and flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[164]</a></sup> About 77,000 residents were left without power at the height of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[165]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Lee">Hurricane Lee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hurricane Lee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Lee 2017-09-27 1450Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg/150px-Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg" width="150" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg/225px-Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg/300px-Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4500" data-file-height="6000" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Lee_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Lee 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lee_2017_track.png/150px-Lee_2017_track.png" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lee_2017_track.png/225px-Lee_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lee_2017_track.png/300px-Lee_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="3000" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 15&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 30</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 962&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave moved off the coast of Africa on September 13. Contrary to predictions of only gradual organization over the following days,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[166]</a></sup> the system rapidly organized, becoming Tropical Depression Fourteen at 03:00&#160;UTC on September 15.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[167]</a></sup> The NHC upgraded the system to Tropical Storm Lee at 15:00&#160;UTC on the next day, based on an increase in deep convection and an <a href="/wiki/Scatterometer" title="Scatterometer">advanced scatterometer</a> (ASCAT) pass which indicated that it was producing minimal tropical-storm-force winds.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[168]</a></sup> After encountering wind shear, Lee gradually weakened into a tropical depression early on September&#160;17 before degenerating into a remnant low two days later.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[170]</a></sup> The NHC monitored the remnants of Lee intermittently for several days, but regeneration was not considered likely.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[172]</a></sup> However, the mid-level remnants of the cyclone became intertwined with an upper-level trough; a deep burst of convection led to a new surface circulation, and by 21:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;22, the system reorganized into Tropical Depression Lee.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[173]</a></sup> It intensified into a tropical storm six hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[174]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A compact cyclone, Lee organized as small curved bands wrapped into a small cluster of central convection.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[175]</a></sup> A microwave pass around 21:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;23 indicated the formation of a ring of shallow to moderate convection around the center, often a harbinger of rapid intensification.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[176]</a></sup> Indeed, by 06:30&#160;UTC the next morning, the presence of an eye on satellite imagery prompted the NHC to abruptly upgrade Lee to a hurricane as it moved erratically.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[177]</a></sup> After attaining winds of 90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h), the storm weakened slightly due to moderate southeasterly wind shear.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[178]</a></sup> By 09:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;26, however, the storm attained Category&#160;2 strength.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[179]</a></sup> An eyewall replacement cycle that night led to the emergence of a larger eye surrounded by cold cloud tops, and by 15:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;27, Lee attained its peak as a Category&#160;3 hurricane with winds of 115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[180]</a></sup> The system recurved northeast after peak intensity and quickly succumbed to strong northerly wind shear and progressively cooler ocean waters;<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[181]</a></sup> it weakened below major hurricane strength by 03:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;28,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[182]</a></sup> fell below hurricane strength by 15:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;29,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[183]</a></sup> and degenerated to a post-tropical cyclone by 09:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;30, after lacking deep convection for over 12 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[184]</a></sup> On October 1, Lee\'s remnant was absorbed by another extratropical cyclone to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-October_1_weather_map_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_1_weather_map-189">[185]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Maria">Hurricane Maria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png" class="image"><img alt="Maria 2017-09-19 2015Z.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png/150px-Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png/225px-Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png/300px-Maria_2017-09-19_2015Z.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1600" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Maria 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/150px-Maria_2017_track.png" width="150" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/225px-Maria_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/300px-Maria_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2290" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 16&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 30</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>175&#160;mph (280&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 908&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a></div>\n<p>On September&#160;13, the NHC began monitoring a tropical wave southwest of Cabo Verde.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[186]</a></sup> The disturbance moved west, organizing into a potential tropical cyclone at 15:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;16 and Tropical Storm Maria six hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[188]</a></sup> On a west-northwest course, Maria intensified at an exceptional rate; over a 24-hour period ending at 23:45&#160;UTC on September&#160;18, Maria doubled its winds from 80&#160;mph (130&#160;km/h) to 160&#160;mph (260&#160;km/h), thus reaching Category&#160;5 strength.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[189]</a></sup> After striking Dominica at that intensity a little over an hour later,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[190]</a></sup> the storm weakened slightly as it entered the eastern Caribbean Sea; amid favorable conditions, however, Maria regained Category&#160;5 intensity and eventually reached peak winds of 175&#160;mph (280&#160;km/h) late on September&#160;19.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[191]</a></sup> Around 08:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;20, the eyewall of Maria struck <a href="/wiki/Vieques" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieques">Vieques</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[192]</a></sup> and a little over two hours later, the core of the storm made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Yabucoa, Puerto Rico</a>, with winds of 155&#160;mph (250&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[193]</a></sup> Land interaction caused a significant degration in Maria\'s structure, and it weakened to a Category&#160;2 hurricane while moving offshore.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[194]</a></sup> Growing in size and curving north, Maria regained Category&#160;3 strength and maintained this intensity for several days before entering a less conducive environment.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[195]</a></sup> After fluctuating between tropical storm and minimal hurricane strength off the coastline of North Carolina,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[196]</a></sup> the system turned sharply east away from the United States, and ultimately evolved into an extratropical cyclone over the far northern Atlantic, on September&#160;30.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[198]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Dominica sustained catastrophic damage from Maria, with nearly every structure on the island damaged or destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[199]</a></sup> Surrounding islands were also dealt a devastating blow, with reports of flooding, downed trees, and damaged buildings. Puerto Rico also suffered catastrophic damage. The island\'s electric grid was devastated, leaving all 3.4 million residents without power. Many structures were leveled, while floodwaters trapped thousands of citizens. The United States National Guard, Coast Guard, Army Corps of Engineers, and other like units worked to administer aid and assist in search and rescue operations. However, the U.S. federal government response was criticized for its delay in waiving the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Marine_Act_of_1920" title="Merchant Marine Act of 1920">Jones Act</a>, a statute which prevented Puerto Rico from receiving aid on ships from non-U.S. flagged vessels. Along the coastline of the United States, tropical storm-force gusts cut power to hundreds of citizens; rip currents offshore led to three deaths and numerous water rescues. Estimates of damage from Maria range from $15.9 billion by Estudios T\xc3\xa9cnicos to $95 billion by <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Analytics" title="Moody\'s Analytics">Moody\'s Analytics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MariaDamageEstimate_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MariaDamageEstimate-204">[200]</a></sup> Most of the damage occurred in Puerto Rico; Ricardo Rossell\xc3\xb3, the governor of Puerto Rico, believes the storm caused $90 billion in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-90_billion_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90_billion-205">[201]</a></sup> The death toll currently stands at 90, with 30 killed in Dominica, 5 in the Dominican Republic, 2 in Guadeloupe, 3 in Haiti, 46 in Puerto Rico, 1 in the United States Virgin Islands, and 4 in the Contiguous United States.<sup id="cite_ref-43_in_Puerto_Rico_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43_in_Puerto_Rico-206">[202]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Nate">Hurricane Nate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hurricane Nate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Nate 2017-10-07 1848Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg/150px-Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg" width="150" height="196" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg/225px-Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg/300px-Nate_2017-10-07_1848Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4808" data-file-height="6272" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Nate_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Nate 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Nate_2017_track.png/150px-Nate_2017_track.png" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Nate_2017_track.png/225px-Nate_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Nate_2017_track.png/300px-Nate_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="3000" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 4&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 October 9</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 981&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nate_(2017)" title="Hurricane Nate (2017)">Hurricane Nate (2017)</a></div>\n<p>On October&#160;3, a broad area of low pressure formed in the southwestern Caribbean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[203]</a></sup> The disturbance quickly organized, and on October 4, the NHC announced that the disturbance had strengthened into Tropical Depression Sixteen, and began issuing advisories on the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[204]</a></sup> The system slowly became stronger and more organized, and, early on October 5, was deemed a tropical storm and named Nate.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[205]</a></sup> Nate\'s first U.S landfall was in the mouth of the Mississippi River as a Category 1 hurricane, and Nate\'s second U.S landfall was at 12:30 a.m. CST near Biloxi, MS, both on October 8. After Nate made its landfalls, Nate quickly weakened into a tropical depression, and a few hours later, Nate evolved into an extratropical storm. Hurricane Nate also broke the record for the fastest moving hurricane ever recorded in the Gulf of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-fastest_storm_in_Gulf_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastest_storm_in_Gulf-210">[206]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Nate caused at least 40 deaths, including 16 in Nicaragua,<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-211">[207]</a></sup> 11 in Costa Rica,<sup id="cite_ref-Bohemia_1006_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bohemia_1006-212">[208]</a></sup> 7 in Panama,<sup id="cite_ref-ElMundo_1006_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElMundo_1006-213">[209]</a></sup> 3 in Honduras,<sup id="cite_ref-ElMundo_1006_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElMundo_1006-213">[209]</a></sup> 1 in El Salvador,<sup id="cite_ref-ElMundo_1006_213-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElMundo_1006-213">[209]</a></sup> and 2 in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[211]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Ophelia">Hurricane Ophelia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Hurricane Ophelia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ophelia 2017-10-14 1454Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg/150px-Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg" width="150" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg/225px-Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg/300px-Ophelia_2017-10-14_1454Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3736" data-file-height="4808" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Ophelia_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Ophelia 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Ophelia_2017_track.png/150px-Ophelia_2017_track.png" width="150" height="108" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Ophelia_2017_track.png/225px-Ophelia_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Ophelia_2017_track.png/300px-Ophelia_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2162" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 9&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 October 16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 960&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">Hurricane Ophelia (2017)</a></div>\n<p>On October&#160;6, a circulation developed at the end of a cold front in the northeast Atlantic, with a low pressure area developing within the circulation on the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[212]</a></sup> While the low drifted slowly to the northeast, it began to lose its frontal system and acquire subtropical characteristics by October 7.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[213]</a></sup> The next day, the storm encountered stronger wind shear, removing some of its convection, and slightly weakening the system; however, the storm eventually grew better organized and developed more convection around its low pressure center later in the day.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[214]</a></sup> Early on October 9, the system fully transitioned into a tropical cyclone, prompting the NHC to begin issuing advisories on Tropical Depression Seventeen.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[216]</a></sup> The tropical depression continued to strengthen, becoming Tropical Storm Ophelia later that day.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[217]</a></sup> Ophelia continued to strengthen due to low wind shear and on October 11, the National Hurricane Center upgraded it to a hurricane, making it the tenth consecutive storm this season to reach hurricane strength.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[218]</a></sup> Ophelia became a Category 2 hurricane on October 12 at 5:00&#160;p.m. AST (21:00 UTC).<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[219]</a></sup> On October 14 at 11:00&#160;a.m. AST (15:00 UTC), Ophelia unexpectedly intensified to a Category 3 hurricane, making Ophelia the sixth major hurricane of the season and the easternmost storm of such strength in the Atlantic basin on record.<sup id="cite_ref-RecordEast_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RecordEast-224">[220]</a></sup> On October 15, Ophelia began to weaken, while accelerating northeastward towards <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, with the storm\'s wind field also expanding. Early on October 16, Ophelia transitioned into a hurricane-strength extratropical cyclone, as it began impacting Ireland and Britain.</p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/County_Waterford" title="County Waterford">County Waterford</a>, a woman was killed when a tree fell on her car, caused by the winds from Ophelia\'s remnants.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[221]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/County_Tipperary" title="County Tipperary">County Tipperary</a>, a man was killed while clearing a fallen tree with a chainsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[222]</a></sup> A third person was killed in <a href="/wiki/Dundalk" title="Dundalk">Dundalk</a> when a tree fell on his car.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[223]</a></sup> Hurricane Ophelia also fanned <a href="/wiki/October_2017_Iberian_wildfires" title="October 2017 Iberian wildfires">wildfires in Portugal and Spain</a>, killing 48 people.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_systems">Other systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg/170px-10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg/255px-10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg/340px-10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5025" data-file-height="7057" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nPotential Tropical Cyclone Ten near the Carolinas on August 28</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>A long-tracked tropical wave was designated as Potential Tropical Cyclone Ten on August 27, while it was located northeast of Florida. The NHC gave this disturbance a 90% chance of becoming a tropical cyclone within the next 48 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[224]</a></sup> The system reached sustained wind speeds of 45 miles per hour and affected the East Coast. However, the system did not attain any more tropical characteristics, and it began to undergo an extratropical transition. Consequently, the NHC issued its last advisory on the system at 21:00 UTC on August 29, declaring the system to be an extratropical low.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[225]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>\n<p>The following list of names will be used for named storms that form in the North Atlantic in 2017. Any retired names will be announced by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO) in the spring of 2018. The names not retired from this list will not be used again until the 2023 season.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[226]</a></sup> This is the same list used in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2011 Atlantic hurricane season">2011 season</a>, with the exception of the name Irma, which replaced <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene" title="Hurricane Irene">Irene</a>; Irma was previously used in the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Irma_(1978)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Irma (1978)">1978 season</a>.</p>\n<table style="width:90%;">\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li>Arlene</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">Bret</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">Cindy</a></li>\n<li>Don</li>\n<li>Emily</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin" title="Hurricane Franklin">Franklin</a></li>\n<li>Gert</li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Harvey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Jose</a></li>\n<li>Katia</li>\n<li>Lee</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Maria</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nate_(2017)" title="Hurricane Nate (2017)">Nate</a></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">Ophelia</a></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Philippe&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Rina&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Sean&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Tammy&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Vince&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Whitney&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>The usage of the name "Don" in July garnered some negative attention relating to <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>. <a href="/wiki/Max_Mayfield" title="Max Mayfield">Max Mayfield</a>, former director of the National Hurricane Center, clarified that the name had no relation to Trump and was chosen in 2006 as a replacement for <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dennis" title="Hurricane Dennis">Dennis</a>. Regardless, some outlets such as the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, "poked fun" at the name and Trump.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[228]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a table of all the storms that have formed in the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, affected areas, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2017 <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">USD</a>.</p>\n<table align="center" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="background:transparent;text-align:center">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="7" nowrap="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale</a></small></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#5ebaff;width:1.8em" title="Tropical Depression: &lt;39 mph (0\xe2\x80\x9362 km/h)">TD</td>\n<td 74\xe2\x80\x9395 mph (118\xe2\x80\x93153 km/h)">C1</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ffe775;width:1.8em" title="Category 2: 96\xe2\x80\x93110 mph (154\xe2\x80\x93177 km/h)">C2</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ffc140;width:1.8em" title="Category 3: 111\xe2\x80\x93130 mph (178\xe2\x80\x93209 km/h)">C3</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ff8f20;width:1.8em" title="Category 4: 131\xe2\x80\x93155 mph (210\xe2\x80\x93249 km/h)">C4</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ff6060;width:1.8em" title="Category 5: \xe2\x89\xa5156 mph (\xe2\x89\xa5250 km/h)">C5</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<table border="1" cellpadding="5" cellspacing="0" class="wikitable">\n<caption style="font-size:100%">2017 <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_tropical_cyclones" class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There is an undercount bias of zero to six tropical cyclones per year between 1851 and 1885 and zero to four per year between 1886 and 1910, due to the lack of modern observation techniques, see <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_observation" title="Tropical cyclone observation">Tropical cyclone observation</a>. This may have led to significantly lower ACE ratings for hurricane seasons prior to 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA1-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NOAA2_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA2-24">[24]</a></sup></span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The totals represent the sum of the squares for every (sub)tropical storm\'s intensity of over 33&#160;knots (38&#160;mph, 61&#160;km/h), divided by 10,000. Calculations are provided at <a href="/wiki/Talk:2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season/ACE_calcs" title="Talk:2017 Atlantic hurricane season/ACE calcs">Talk:2017 Atlantic hurricane season/ACE calcs</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It should be noted that Arlene would likely not have been detected without the help of satellites, and there may well have been other similar storms this early in the year in the pre-satellite era (1966 and before).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup></span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-129"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-129">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Higher rainfall totals occurred during the <a href="/wiki/1909_Greater_Antilles_hurricane" title="1909 Greater Antilles hurricane">Greater Antilles hurricane</a> of 1909; peaking at 135.00&#160;in (3,429&#160;mm) in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Flora" title="Hurricane Flora">Hurricane Flora</a> of 1963; peaking at 100.39&#160;in (2,550&#160;mm) in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. For more information, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country" title="List of wettest tropical cyclones by country">List of wettest tropical cyclones by country</a>.</span></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://science.sciencemag.org/content/293/5529/474.full">"The Recent Increase in Atlantic Hurricane Activity: Causes and Implications | Science"</a>. <i>ScienceMag</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
